REVIEW #16
================================================================================
User: Rudra
Steam ID: 76561197962405793
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.8 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 20, 2022

Posted: May 20, 2022
																Loved the original, and this updated version is just as good.The additions along the way are very nice, and the improved graphics are noticeable. Being able to converse with your partners whenever you want is also amazing.However...Was disappointed to have a few areas and puzzles removed. Since those were the more difficult parts of the original game, I assume this was done for a more streamlined experience. Instead of your flower wilting to represent your life, it is now replaced by more accurate "points". Although this makes it easier to tell exactly how many hits you can take, I miss the more original old design.An iconic music track was also changed, likely due to licensing issues... Can't completely replace the original for me, but it's still a very worthwhile experience! Still wishing for a sequel a decade later.

REVIEW #29

User:  ö ‚ô° Sarahtonin ‚ô° …û
Steam ID: 76561198111288547
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 5.3 hrs on record
Date: Posted: April 20, 2022

Posted: April 20, 2022
																Words honestly can't describe how much I just genuinely love this game. I remember when I first heard about it by watching PewDiePie play it back in 2012, and ever since then it's been my all time favorite RPG Maker game. I spent probably 200+ hours just replaying it over and over again, I have no idea what it was about Ib, but the kid me was just so in love with this game. I had the soundtrack on my PSP which I carried everywhere and listened to often, I replayed the game what had to have been at least over 100 times, and I was there for Every update. I remember when the Extra Dungeon update dropped and I was so excited, I had thought the game wasn't gonna be getting anything new, and there the Extra Dungeon update came in. I kept doing the steps to unlock the Dungeon wrong, and I ended up replaying the entire game 4 times in one day, Just to get to that Dungeon, because I wanted to play through it so bad. I had known about other RPG Maker games before, but Ib was the one that Really stood out to me, and got me into the rest. Ib is one of my biggest inspirations for wanting to make my own unique and bizarre games, and stories. There's just so much I could say about what this game has done for me, but I'm sure I'd run out of space to type, honestly. When I read that there was a Remake coming to Steam, I was beyond excited. If not for an excuse to replay the game once again, then for the fact that I'd get to hopefully see the game with some new ideas and changes that Kouri would have wanted to make to the game. It was all just so exciting to me. I bought it as soon as I could, and even though it's not in English yet, I still played through the game as best I could. When I couldn't use my memory to complete stuff, I would try my best to translate the dialogue into English. It was so much fun revisiting this game, the new artwork, new puzzles, new ideas, and just generally, everything about this remake warms my little heart, and brings such a big smile to my face. I imagine now that I've gotten back into this game, I'm gonna be replaying it over and over again, just like I did back in 2012-2015. What else can I say? This game holds the most special place in my heart, and it will always mean the world to me. I'm really grateful that this came to steam, and I'm honestly really grateful this remake happened at all! What a pleasant surprise. I'm just so uncontrollably happy, Thank you so much Kouri for making one of my most Favorite games of all time, I really hope to see more from you in the future, and I am extremely glad, and happy to see you still around. You're my hero! ^w^ ‚ô•

================================================================================
REVIEW #37
================================================================================
User: Aosakai
Steam ID: 76561198042334706
Recommendation: Negative
Hours Played: 4.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 19, 2022

Posted: May 19, 2022
																This review was initially framed for veterans of IB who have played the original and want to know if the Steam version is worth the price over the original, as well as if this version is the definitive version of IB. I will also remark on if new players should buy this version at the end of the review over the free version. This review is a bullet-point list of things better, mixed, or worse compared to the free version. If you are a new player, you can skip just to the conclusion to avoid spoilers.Exceptionally better:-You can talk with Garry at any moment in almost every room (and with different dialogues depending on different location within the room, so a huge chunk of new dialogue). This is - by far - exceptional fan-service since one of the biggest draws for fans to buy an expanded version of games they've completed is to spend more time with characters they love, and you have that in spades with this version. Alongside Garry, Mary also has this expanded dialogue as well when she's in your party. -IB's dream (nightmare) sequence right after the end of the Grey Area is executed more artfully and a better and richer dream sequence overall.Better:-So much level streamlining, rooms that did not need to be rooms are deleted and some puzzles are streamlined on unnecessary aspects (6 tile pieces instead of 12). Not all of this is better, but quite a bit are an improvement.-Characters have better portraits, especially Mary who has a cute fang now when she's angry at you.-The top-down pixel art is better overall, but there is some minor inferiorities here and there (the blue dolls in the bunny room are slightly less intimidating than the free version)-True Exhibit picture tracking is streamlined across save files, so the game remembers which picture you've already seen not just from inside one single save-file line, but across all save files (as long as you saved).Mixed:-The puzzles overall. Quite a few puzzles have been replaced for completely new puzzles and many original puzzles that were kept were streamlined in some ways. On the whole, I personally felt the new puzzles are easier than the old puzzles, either more obvious or just less steps, and I don't like this. The new puzzles are not as interesting as the old ones, but they are more streamlined and less prone to getting new players stuck on a step, but I don't mind if the player gets stuck on a good puzzle because it's ultimately worth it. The whole vent-logic of the rainbow pallet area is replaced with some snake and vent orientation puzzle which is less imaginative and clever for me. Some players might prefer these slightly easier and more streamlined puzzles, but I don't.Worse:-Grey Area escalation sequence, the new version is a scripted linear maze where you flee from a single painting compared to the free version where it is utter chaos with every monster coming to life at the same time and you have absolutely no idea where you are going. In this new version, Garry immediately points you to the exit before the monster chases you so there is no uncertainty, but in the old version it's utter confusion and panic since you don't initially know where to go and everything has come alive trying to kill you. This new version is so inferior to the old version it blows my mind that Kouri removed it, this is one of the tensest moments of the original game and now it's nowhere near as tense or memorable.-Excessive puzzle hints. In certain areas, not all, there are too many hints to be gained from just talking to your companion character, whether it's Gary or Mary. You will have hints all the way through to the finish line, Kouri doesn't want any player to be left behind which is noble in some regard, but I see great value in letting players get stuck and having to push themselves to figure it out. By getting stuck, the puzzles become a bigger achievement since the players had to work harder for the solution, so hints that guide through the entire puzzle undermine the satisfaction in a real way. This doesn't always happen, but it does happen. -Music. Kouri switched around which tracks are played during which scenes (some not all), and also replaced some tracks with completely new songs. This was never done in a way that improved upon the original free version, there was not a single switch or new song that was better than the track and scene matching of the original, so it's just overall worse.-Rpgmaker Engine version. MV is a lot buggier than Rpgmaker 2000, so there will be a longer period of bug-crunching to make it as bug-free as the free version. I encountered a bug that forced me to restart the game once during my playthrough. There have been several patches now, so it should in theory be better.A lot worse:-Sound effects. I am so sad that the very aggressive "HWAA!!" that the red headless statue shouts at you when it comes alive is removed and replaced with silence. Really Kouri? Why? That sound effect alone establishes the danger and urgency for running away from the monster so strongly for the game, and you removed or changed this central aspect of tension not just from the first red statue, but also for the black hands coming out of the walls and the red lady as well. This dilutes the horror so much, it was central for establishing tension inside the initial monster encounters and how could you possibly remove this sound effect? I am baffled that Kouri who created the original IB is the same person who made this remake that doesn't see the value of these sound effects.Conclusion: Overall, if you are a big fan of IB and have played the free version many times before, just the fact that you have so many new lines of optional dialogue with Gary should alone be enough to make you purchase the Steam version so I can recommend it to veterans who love and are passionate about the original game. But is this the Definitive version of IB? I would say No it is not because the puzzles, while more streamlined, are less rewarding and imaginative than the original and more importantly, the horror is inferior to the free version because of some decisions of redesigning events as well as removing certain sound effects that set the tension. The Definitive version is still the freeware version 1.07.So for new players that have never played IB, the better experience is within the original free version so I recommend playing that over buying this. For veteran players, the game is worth it for the expanded time and dialogue with Gary and a nice trip down memory lane inside this beloved game. I would like to give a mixed review rather than a binary thumb up or down, but for the sake of new players I will thumb it down.

REVIEW #46
================================================================================
User: Patreii | „É§„É≥„Éá„É¨
Steam ID: 76561198088891313
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 11.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: February 17, 2024

Posted: February 17, 2024
																As someone who has fond memories of playing the accessible version of Ib about ten years ago, I was over the moon once I heard it was released on Steam. This horror visual novel about Ib, a little girl caught in the illusion of a museum alongside Garry, surprised me with its engaging storyline and appealing characters.The game conjures an exciting world that one would very much like to explore, to unlock the said world's mysteries, and also to understand its history. Ib, Garry, and Mary themselves bring layers to the story, making each interaction meaningful and every session of solving the different puzzles satisfying. Even though the puzzles might prove somewhat problematic, they continue to balance not being too challenging to complete and allowing a good gameplay experience."Ib" is a game that is going subtle on horror: no sudden scares, no overpowering gore. Instead, it builds up that feeling of unease and fear as the story progresses. Creepy encounters with disturbing artwork and the strangeness of the museum keep players on edge without giving away cheap thrills.The Steam version of "Ib" is updated with several enhancements that make the overall gameplay experience better. With better graphics and dialogue screens, up to the ability to talk to the game's companions whenever you like, these editions help make the game more immersive and further aid one in building a stronger bond with the characters in the game. Sometimes, the puzzles change; generally, the changes favor better game mechanics, yet some classics may upset die-hard enthusiasts.This is a vital aspect of the game that raises feelings while it raises introspection. I had an episode of depression at that time, which brought many thoughts to the fore concerning love, loneliness, and time. The moving soundtrack, which I still listen to for inspiration, further added the depth of emotional experience while playing the game.In the end, "Ib" is more an artwork than a horror game; it resonates profoundly and stays beautifully created for the ones who get to partake in its enigma. Be you picking it back up again after years or new to the experience, this is a journey well worth taking, one that will stay with you long after you finish playing.Also, it might be a bit controversial, but I totally loved Mary as a character and the 'Together Forever' ending is definitely my favorite one <3

REVIEW #49
================================================================================
User: CollateralDamageMan
Steam ID: 76561197998694045
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 1.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: February 10, 2023

Posted: February 10, 2023
																Ib manages to do for me what so few horror games manage to accomplish, and that is to actually give a sense of unease and dread. Without going into spoilers, it's only a few minutes into the game that things start to tread the path of uncomfortable surrealism, with the art growing considerably more disturbing in how Ib interacts with it, and how the art interacts with her.With all due respect to more conventional horror titles, say, Dead Space or The Evil Within, Ib maintains a feeling of dread and discomfort. Enemies can be evaded, yes, but there's a feeling of being stalked while trapped in a world you can't possibly fully understand. Contrast Dead Space remake, where soon enough the horror gives way to cutting off an abomination's arm, then using telekinesis to impale it or another horror with said arm, then simply setting fire to the more mobile enemies.This is not, I repeat, not to disrespect games in which reducing enemies to a smoldering heap of charred body parts is an acceptable tactic- there is a time and a place for the cathartic destruction of the nightmares that haunted our closets and lurked under our beds. Ib, however, leans firmly towards the horror and self-preservation of being in a hostile and unknown environment, where the only feasible option is to run, hide, and hope whatever nameless horror eventually loses track of you.And let's face it- some modern art galleries are creepy enough already, even in the daylight.

REVIEW #58
================================================================================
User: Quinn the Padoru
Steam ID: 76561198122244584
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 9.0 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 18, 2022

Posted: May 18, 2022
																How do I even go about reviewing this? Of all the rpgmaker titles in my library, from Ao Oni to Mad Father to The Witch's House to Corpse Party, The Crooked Man or even To The Moon, none have hit that level of being an absolute icon in the rpgmaker/indie horror fandom. Well, all those other ones are actually franchises more or less now, so I guess that claim is debatable. But Ib itself become the posterchild up there with the others for the big rpgmaker horror boom that took over gaming-YouTube circa 2012. And for good reason!The music, the characters, the aesthetics, the endings, all absolute classics looking back, which I was more than happy to relive 10 years later. It absolutely held up.Like other Steam versions of these games, these are remakes you pay for as opposed to the freeware we downloaded years ago. It has all the most recent content (including extra dungeons and endings that people who played before 1.04 may not have seen!) with updated graphics and UI, and quite honestly I am more than happy to pay this creator regardless.Exploring everything Ib can be a little headscratching at times. You'll want a guide handy to explore all the endings, or even just to get the best ending because the requirements for forming emotional bonds (or doom) with your party members can be pretty strict. And as a personal note, it's my opinion that the health meter is a little harder to read than in the original.That being said, save smartly, and you can see everything in 2-3 playthroughs and roughly 8 hours of playtime, going by my stats, roughly 2 hours per route. A short, sweet horror that people love to death as the little darling of the genre, and I am counted among them. I can't see myself not naming this as one of my favorite games at any point in the future, distant or not. Just... look at them beautiful pixels!

																I remember playing the free game 10 years ago and simply being sucked into the game. She and another poor soul who gets trapped in this world (Garry) now must navigate through this world and find a way back to their reality. This game gives us a very fascinating world that makes you want to explore it as much as you can, as well as know why it even exists, it has also a great set of characters such as Ib, Garry, and Mary who also are this game is great, and the puzzles itself are rather nice to solve, a bit of a challenge but nothing too difficult. It also has 7 endings in total.Horror-wise, Ib is pretty light in that department, no jump scares or gore, it does have a couple of chase scenes but overall nothing too terrifying. This paid steam version, adds a lot of improvements like, bigger resolution, clearer artwork, the ability to zoom in the screen, better dialogue screens, and my most favorite feature, the ability to talk to your companion anytime in the game. The characters are part of what makes Ib great and being able to talk to Garry at any time was an added bonus. It definitely enhanced the game.Some puzzles were modified, which for some I did not mind (it was an improvement) and for others, I felt disappointed but it's not a deal-breaker.Overall, I definitely recommend anyone to buy Ib, it's a great game that will suck you in.

REVIEW #70
================================================================================
User: sLaughter
Steam ID: 76561198046160311
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.2 hrs on record
Date: Posted: August 14, 2022

Posted: August 14, 2022
																Played the free version a long time ago and bought this on short notice after the announcement of an EN translation. I expected it to be the same old game with "higher res" sprites, but it had more to it than I thought.For one, the revamped puzzles are less number-heavy and more dynamic; certain puzzles are never the same from one playthrough after another. Being able to talk to the party members is also a big highlight considering the game's characters; if you're all about that character interaction, this version has you covered while you backtrack. Qualities of Life are also welcome, such as the game not spamming "You don't know this word" after the first time you see it, easier ways to get back to the title screen and/or reload, the  True Exhibitaccurately pointing out how many artworks are available. These are all a refreshing take especially if you're trying to get all artworks and endings.A notable change is the  dream sequence. Genuinely surprised me with the fake save point and rose. Sadly some nuances from the original were lost along the way; certain sound effects were completely changed in favor of being "less scary" such as the wall hands, the wooden fish puzzle, and even damage effects. The revamped layout also pushed certain events out of the way  such as the gallery itself panicking in crayon the first time Garry uses his lighter . Minor details, but in a game like this, details matter.While I like the simplified puzzles, we ended up losing steps along the way, notably in the bonus dungeon on your second run.  The Orange Area no longer needs the star candy for the key to the Cyan Area; the "night" version of two paintings are easy to miss this way. The Cyan Area's Guertena pieces have also been reduced from 12 to 6.  A shame, because the puzzles are a big highlight for a creative game. I simply wish there was more in it, minus the numbers.Overall, the remake is worth picking up, whether you're a freeware veteran or a newcomer just for the sheer amount of creativity put into it. How often do you see art museum-themed games with clever solutions and endearing characters?P.S. Fix the grammar on the only achievement this game has.

REVIEW #79
================================================================================
User: Doctor Professor Fact Core
Steam ID: 76561198049420453
Recommendation: Negative
Hours Played: 11.7 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 16, 2022

Posted: June 16, 2022
																It's with heavy heart that i have to leave a negative review. The original Ib was one of my first loves in regards to RPG horror and i was so excited for this remaster, only to feel a little disappointed.Having gotten all the endings and completed the gallery, i can say it is not worth the $12 price tag.Many iconic things from the sounds the hands make coming out of the walls to Mary's original theme are gone for no apparent reason. Additionally, there are changes such as the UI for the roses which now clashes with the aesthetic of the game. Finally, there are no additional dungeons or endings to help give you reason to further explore the game, instead only giving you the gallery which is a little tedious and doesn't provide much reward. There are some quality of life changes that are greatly appreciated: mostly changing obtuse puzzle solutions. The ability to talk to Garry and Mary when in your party to get little dialogues is also nice and cute and a good way to encourage a little backtracking.It's worth mentioning that graphically, there isn't much difference between this version and the OG. The biggest difference is mostly the CGs looking nicer in the remake. Sprites look a little better but are not mind blowing. Unless there is a massive addition to the game, If you have to buy it, buy it on sale.

(without the horror part ofc) thanks for helping me discover my fav art style and making this remaster to the beautiful game. Hands down the second of my fav games just below tf2.

REVIEW #89
================================================================================
User: Snoobicus
Steam ID: 76561198070031764
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.8 hrs on record
Date: Posted: April 20

Posted: April 20
																RPG maker is a deceptively powerful medium and makes for stories that are more compelling than you'd ever think. Ib is no exception. I took the time a year or two to play the RPG horror classics like Ao Oni, Misao, The Witch's House, and Mad Father, all of which I had only watched on YouTube when they became popular more than a decade ago. Although all of them are precious, Ib is the most charming. The game takes no more than two hours to complete and accomplishes so much in that short period of time. There are seven endings in the game, each of them heart wrenchers which are a testament to how simple yet excellent the atmosphere and narrative is. The changes in this remaster to the decade old freeware edition only serve to further improve upon the original, a relief as remasters and remakes so often fall short and become misguided. The game holds artistic merit the same way an early silent film would, both limited by technical resources but not by imagination and creativity. Everyone should play this classic.

REVIEW #99
================================================================================
User: Hard as a Coffin Nail
Steam ID: 76561198825363604
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 6.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: September 15, 2022

Posted: September 15, 2022
																Ib is a remake of kouri's 2012 RPG Maker horror game of the same name, though odds are you're already aware of that if you're here. Regardless, whether or not you've played Ib before, you've likely heard of it if you have any interest in RPG Maker games. It's an RPG Maker classic, and for good reason. Everything about this game is masterfully done. The spritework is charming, the soundtrack is ambient and eerie, and the story is engaging and bittersweet. Being an RPG without any battles, there's not much to talk about in terms of gameplay, though there are a healthy handful of puzzles scattered about the museum you'll be traversing, and the atmosphere is so cohesive and captivating that the simplistic gameplay won't bother you much anyways. This version of the game has been entirely remade in RPG Maker MV, with all new sprites for absolutely everything, uncompressed music tracks, and even a few new puzzles and areas here and there. However, the changes aren't drastic... certainly nothing that necessitates playing this remake, I would say. It's about 95% the same game. It's definitely a fun new way to play through Ib if you've played the original before, and if you're a new fan, you won't be missing out on much by playing this over the RPG Maker 2003 version. I cannot stress how much I don't want to dissuade anyone from buying this remake, as Ib is still a fantastic game either way and kouri deserves all the support he can get, but I would only do so if you've tried the freeware version first and enjoyed it. They are so similar that there's no real reason not to, unless you just really want to burn through 12 bucks. If you DO end up liking Ib, however, definitely consider buying this remake. It's a great and easy way to throw a few dollars kouri's way and show him some appreciation for putting out one of the most iconic and memorable RPG Maker titles ever.

Some features may be unavailable.Please specify a different profile directory or use some newer version of NW.js".To fix this:- Right click on Ib in library- Go to properties --> installed files --> browse local files- FInd "package.json" and open it in Notepad- Where it says "name", put "Ib" into the second set of quote marks- Save and exitYour game should now be clean!

																I've always been a huge fan of IB ever since I was young. I played both the remastered and the old version of the game and I can confidently say my opinion overall stays the same. The overall design of the game is veryyy good like the main menu, the map and mostly some of the work of arts inside the map. I highly recommend this game to those who are starting out with these kinds of games, but even if you're not, I still recommend it!!

If you're a horror fan then this game is definitely for you as it provides one of the best horror experiences out there.

REVIEW #130
================================================================================
User: metalweeve
Steam ID: 76561198993734741
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 6.7 hrs on record
Date: Posted: July 11, 2024

Posted: July 11, 2024
																Been playing Ib ever since the old version came out, it's safe to say I've replayed this game for over 100 times, so comparing the two made me notice some things that I wish they would have added in this version as well. (Don't focus on the time spent on this game from Steam, I only found out about it being available here today)First of all, I'm really pleased with the graphics improvement, and the ability to zoom so we can see paintings even closer. Being able to chat with Garry and Mary throughout the rooms is another bonus that I really enjoyed, it made the game more immersive and gave us more depth to the character's relationships with each other. However, with the improved graphics also came some negative aspects, where some of the paintings do not seem as eerie as they used to in the previous version. Take the lady who smiles after Ib takes her first key for example. She is no longer creepy, but rather...just cute. Another thing that bugged me was the fact that the hands from the green and yellow room now no longer produced a sound that I found in the old version scary at first, it really added to the horror aspect of the game. Speaking of sounds, again as you're chased by the statues and ladies in the paintings, the sound effect no longer has an impact that had you feeling like you were actually running away from something. Mary's theme also changed, but maybe that's just my nostalgia that's speaking that prefers it over the new tune, but I don't mind that change that much since the melody is also nice. The thing that I did really like was the addition of another Lady in the painting with white hair and hollow eyes, which made perhaps the toughest (tough is a hard word, but compared to other rooms it is tougher to complete) level even better, and I really liked other new artworks, such as Porcupuss and Guardian of Time, although I wish some of the things from the older version still remained in the game, such as the maze which helped you raise your points with Gary.All and all, I still adore this game, and it has been my obsession for the longest time ever so the remake was, in my opinion, much needed to bring people back to this masterpiece.Will absolutely be playing again. 11/10

REVIEW #140
================================================================================
User: keaton
Steam ID: 76561198104091985
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 3.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: January 22, 2023

Posted: January 22, 2023
																The 2022 remake of Ib is a solid remake of an amazing game.This game's story, characters, and beautiful art have been an inspiration to me for years. The atmosphere is fantastic and the distinctive visual style is a lot of fun. Just looking at all the bizarre paintings is a motivation to continue in itself. As someone who grew up with this game, I obviously have a lot of investment in the original game.The rest of this review is less about the game itself and more about its' quality as a remake.I can say without doubt that this version is definitively the best. There is now a button to press for dialogue with characters in your party at any time, and it's a nice treat to get new dialogue for them. The graphical quality has received a nice little boost, and it's easier to tell what some of the paintings are supposed to depict now.Some of the puzzles are slightly less obtuse, meaning this version might be more accessible.I'm not fully convinced that all of the improvements truly justify replacing the original version, though. Ib (2012) is still available online, completely for free. There are no major flaws that needed to be addressed by a remake, and the experience really isn't that different. The only change that I'm truly not fond of is the health bar. Ib (2012) had a picture of your character's rose in the corner, with the visual state of the rose showing your character's state. If the rose wilts, so too will you rot away. However, in Ib (2022) that visual has been replaced with a symbolic rose icon, where your health is instead represented by thorns. This change weakens the impact of the rose in the story; Visually seeing the rose lose its' petals gave you more of a connection to the characters' situation.Other than a few paintings missing, that is the biggest problem I have with Ib (2022). Rather small compared to the good changes, but as a long-time fan, I feel that the iconography of the rose is important to the game. All of that being said, Ib (2022) is most certainly best version of Ib, and personally I'm happy that the game is getting more attention. In any form, this game will be a good time, and if you want to pay 10 dollars for the small improvements then I see no reason not to, because this game is good.(I have currently only completed the main route of the game; If there is more to be said about subsequent playthroughs and post-game content then I will be sure to come back and re-make this review.)

REVIEW #141
================================================================================
User: Kenstagator
Steam ID: 76561199147028014
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 22.9 hrs on record
Date: Posted: August 1, 2023

Posted: August 1, 2023
 Ib: A Cult Classic Gem That Still Shines You know, I have a soft spot for indie horror adventure games, and when it comes to classics, Ib holds a special place in my heart. I mean, it's been over a decade since its original freeware release, and it's still as captivating as ever. Now, with this remake on RPG Maker MV, I was a bit skeptical, wondering if it would retain the whimsy and charm of the original or fall prey to the dreaded soulless remake curse. But boy, was I pleasantly surprised.From the get-go, Ib sets the stage with a strange and unsettling art exhibit that pulls you right into the madness of artist Weiss Guertena. The atmosphere is eerie, the puzzles are creative yet challenging, and the characters, though brief in appearance, are endearing and fully fleshed out. While it may not have traditional RPG elements like combat or character progression, its meaningful story and multiple endings make it a standout in the adventure game genre.As you guide Ib through this bizarre world, you can't help but feel the influence of Alice in Wonderland. But believe me, Guertena's world is darker, claustrophobic, and far deadlier. Yet, it's so wonderfully appealing with its weird and whimsical art style. The way the bizarre creations come to life is both captivating and unsettling, and the use of crayons in certain scenes adds to its childlike charm.One of the things I love about Ib is that it knows how to build tension without relying on combat. Running from foes, solving puzzles, and avoiding danger keeps you on your toes. The difficulty is forgiving, and the generous autosave ensures that failure is a learning experience rather than a punishment.The haunting music and spot-on sound effects make the whole experience even more immersive. The eerie soundtrack perfectly complements the creepy ambiance and adds feelings of loneliness and helplessness. It's easily one of the game's strongest points.Sure, Ib's gameplay may be simple, but that's what makes it so compelling. The interactions with the characters may be limited, but they quickly become memorable. And despite the short playtime, the game packs a punch with its multiple endings, which can be a bit tricky to figure out without some help.As a fan of indie RPG Maker horror games, Ib was a delightful journey into the past‚Äîa golden era of creativity within a limited toolset. It's a testament to what independent developers can achieve when they let their imagination run wild.So, in conclusion, Ib is a special little gem that still holds its charm over a decade later. With its haunting aesthetic, unique world design, and clever puzzles, it's a must-play for horror fans and adventure game enthusiasts alike. Sure, it may have its quirks like the unexplained bond mechanic for certain endings, and the controls might feel a bit stiff, but those are minor bumps in an otherwise fantastic experience.If you're looking for a short and sweet adventure that leaves a lasting impression, Ib is the way to go. It's well worth your time and money, and I highly recommend diving into this eerie and captivating world.

REVIEW #150
================================================================================
User: RattyRattington
Steam ID: 76561198045655521
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 14.9 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 24, 2022

Posted: May 24, 2022
																The beloved 2012 RPG Maker classic Ib is back. I highly recommend it for old-time players seeking to relive the nostalgia and new players alike.Some of the key differences in this remake are some of the level layouts and puzzles being changed, removed and even brand new additions to make the Art Gallery make more sense and be less difficult and more streamlined. The graphics have also been improved and a zoom mode was added which I didn't use much, but it's cool that it exists. Plenty of UI changes/art improvements too.However the best feature of this remake in my opinion is the talk to your partner feature. It's really interesting hearing Garry's thoughts and opinions on various areas, events and puzzles and learning a bit more about him (Mary too!) and seeing their relationship with Ib. A TON of dialogue has been added via this feature alone, I recommend using it alot. It primarily feels like fanservice for old-time Ib players and might be a bit tedious to new players though but it adds alot of life to the game. I just kept talking to Garry after doing literally anything lol.Oh and a useful piece of advice to keep in mind is that there's an achievement for seeing all 150 of Guertena's artworks, so be sure to interact with everything (and with Garry present if possible since they don't count if Ib's 9 year-old brain can't understand the words).There's a few minor downsides(?) in my opinion, though I don't even know if I'd actually complain about them, but I thought I'd list them anyway. The UI is different and while I'm all for it, I do miss the old health system of seeing the rose decay and wilt with missing petals the more damage you've taken instead of the color just fading like it does now. Mary's theme also seems to have changed due to copyright, but I ended up warming up to her new theme in the end. There's also a chase sequence which was alot more intense on the old version (loads more enemies), but it's super dumbed down and easy on the remake.Basically Ib modernized but a bit more easy with some additional features and some new content. Interesting for old and new players. The original is still free, so you could always just play that too. If you're brand new to Ib, you could go with either version honestly but it's nice to support the creator after such a great game being free all this time.

I still find new things every day and I can't wait to keep playing more.Thank you to everyone who worked on this game, it brings me so much happiness each and every time I open to play it.

REVIEW #180
================================================================================
User: Marzipan
Steam ID: 76561199024315136
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 14.9 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 30, 2023

Posted: May 30, 2023
																I only saw footage of the original so this first comment is a guess:The remake looks easier and smoother. The horror elements and story are truthfully ported apparently.Bad parts first:Fetch quest chores can overwhelm, some hidden object quest drown in background colours and active elements and hints appear too random to solve the riddle, very rarely though. (Twice in my case)Low replay value as commonly in story-driven games. Experience puzzles and scares once, then speedrun re-attempts since nothing changes which is kinda boring.The game also doesn't clearly specify how and when your choices matter.Good parts:The atmosphere is pretty good, horror elements keep the player engaged and there are a lot of interesting and clever little interactions. Controls are simple, the game is tight, linear. Art, music and story are decent.The biggest shock I had was figuring out that CHOICES MATTER for the MULTIPLE ENDINGS.Good focus on few key characters and not tons of empty husks.The game hits different. It's pretty chill and could be way more horror and less linear puzzle game.That said it was an absolute treat to play and didn't overstay it's welcome with weird achievement grinds.Essentually another glorified walking simulator, it does a mighty fine job being memorable. Big thumbs up.

REVIEW #188
================================================================================
User: The Arkhom Destroyer
Steam ID: 76561198954800890
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 6.2 hrs on record
Date: Posted: October 22

Posted: October 22
																One of the many remade RPGMaker classics that have been a common place in the late 2010s to the 2020s. I had this game since last Christmas I think and decided to play though for this spooky time of year. I wouldn't say Ib is as scary as its contemporaries such as Mad Father or Witch's House (Hell, I'd say this game isn't really scary at all) but it does beat its competition in style and atmosphere. The Fabricated World is strange and surreal, nothing is as it seems and you're always wondering where Guertena's mind was in each and every single one of his art pieces, especially Mary and his self portrait. The dynamics between the main trio is fun and makes you wish all three could see the world outside the the fabrication. The music is also really solid, ranging from creepy music box tunes, to dreary ambiance, to soothing acapella guitar songs. The only real complaint I have is that the the Health Indicator isn't as used in the remake isn't as cool as the one used in the original, the visual of Ib or Garry's roses falling apart as they take damage is way better than a rose icon losing color. Ib's earned it place in the RPG maker community as one of the classics and it nice to see Playism brought it to a new audiance.

REVIEW #197
================================================================================
User: bottolo
Steam ID: 76561198111637288
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 5.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: October 17, 2022

Posted: October 17, 2022
																Ib, an evergreen. I remember watching videos on YouTube and playing this many, many years ago. It was huge, everyone talked about it and it led to a series of successes to similar games such as Misao, Mad Father, The Crooked Man, To The Moon etc. If you were around during the gaming landscape in the early 2010s, you knew about Ib. It was really creative then, and to many degrees it still is now.Preview of Ib below, if you want to support my channel. I upload videos to support my reviews!


YouTube‚Ñ¢ Video: ¬†

			Views: 0		



When I saw that Ib was coming to Steam, I just had to wishlist it. It's been at least 10 years since I played this.Always ThereI felt I've never really forgot about this game, since everything felt so familiar when I began playing. And that's because your first playthrough will be exactly as you remember it to be. The only real differences are of course some mild added mechanics such as a simple zoom in to further look at the various paintings or characters.The gameplay is exactly the same: a linear adventure with various puzzle elements, easy but satisfying to solve. You  can talk with your "allies" while walking around various areas, and there's quite a lot of dialogue. Speaking of which, dialogues are not particularly complex and for the most part they fall flat and feel sometimes too "anime-ish". Ib's strength is not found in how dialogues are written, rather than the experience and the atmosphere it manages to put you in, which for me makes up for everything else. On the other hand, though, art description is well made and interesting to read all the way through.What's IbThe premise is rather simple. You're with your parents and you're going to visit an exhibition of various art pieces made by the fictional artist Guertena. While exploring around the area, strange things begin to happen and suddenly you'll be introduced to an otherworldly section where you'll have to find an exit in order to survive. This, of course, isn't Ib's main focus. The whole core concept is based upon art, and it's safe to say that it delivers in such sense through the interestingly vivid yet minimalistic Guertena works. The subtle animations give depth to the things you see and manage to describe the artist very well. Even though many years have passed, I have to say that Ib doesn't lose itself while going forward, meaning that art will always be the main concern with the plot. So much so that the plot revolves around that in every sense, but I won't tell you why since I don't want to spoil everything. :)To sum it up, the art direction on this game is clear and manages to be coherent all the way through, with various interesting ideas scattered here and there, and an atmosphere which will always be remembered. I haven't said anything about the score, I know. I'll just say that the melodies of Ib are echoing in my mind since I've first booted it up. I think that speaks for itself. Moody, warm, deep and "Rule of Rose"-sque. It captures well the whole "rose" deal they came up with.New Content?I'll admit that having the possibility to get other endings is exciting and I'm willing to go through the story one more time to discover additional areas. The fact that after so many years we've gotten new content in Ib is really cool, and I can't wait to play more. I'll eventually update this review after I've done a second playthrough.With that said, I can't recommend this enough. It's an interesting game, and it's basically history. It's a must have for people who liked games such as Yume Nikki, Misao, The Witch House or To The Moon. If you're into those kind of games, you won't be disappointed, trust me on this! If you've played this in the past, I still recommend buying it to support the developer as well as enjoy the new content which has been added.More reviews:https://steamcommunity.com/id/bodolovsello/recommendedYT:https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCXMd490dpLAJxONpEpvOMnw

																One of the game's main strengths is its ability to create a pervasive sense of unease and tension, achieved through expert design of the environment, music, and sound effects. If you're looking for a game that will keep you on edge and fully immersed in its world, IB is definitely worth checking out on Steam.

REVIEW #221
================================================================================
User: vampra3
Steam ID: 76561198799248308
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 13.1 hrs on record
Date: Posted: April 19, 2024

Posted: April 19, 2024
																I first played the original Ib back in 2017. It is one of my favorite games of all time! I remember this game was still a bit obscure and lacked much of a fandom or even merch, despite it being such a staple for the RPG horror genre. When I heard it was getting a remake, I was ON it. This version didn't disappoint. Polished graphics, expanded dialogue, fixed puzzles, and extra content! It changed quite a bit but still had the same charm. It was like playing it for the first time again. The bonus dungeon and the True Exhibit gallery were awesome additions to this game, I spent two days making sure I completed everything for the steam achievement. If you've never played Ib, YOU NEED TO! Especially if you're a fan of other RPG horror games like The Witch's House, Mad Father, etc. It's a bit on the shorter side, but the characters are so well-written and unforgettable. The music and the atmosphere is one of a kind and will have you fully immersed into it's strange world, but I won't say too much so you can experience it for yourself. I can tell the creator put so much love and passion into the game's story, characters, art, and mechanics. You might feel pretty emotional by the time you've completed all the endings of the game, so bring tissues. And again, PLAY IB!! You won't regret it! <3

REVIEW #248
================================================================================
User: Schoell
Steam ID: 76561198253298731
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 16, 2023

Posted: May 16, 2023
																Ib is a really interesting and oddly charming Puzzle Adventure Horror game!Its got a really unsettling atmosphere throughout thanks to its soundtrack and really unique art. The puzzle solving mostly is also really good too with every solution feeling really intuitive if you've been paying attention, but also unique and clever with it making really good use of its setting as an art gallery. Many of the horror elements I also found really fascinating more than anything and the overall narrative was pretty dang solid!and most importantly: GarryI do however have a minor gripe with this game when replaying it. After finishing it, you already know the answers to all of the game's puzzles since all of them have a set solution. This wouldn't normally be much of a problem but  the game has multiple endings, encouraging you to play through it multiple times. A lot of the endings also have very specific conditions that are extremely easy to miss. I recommend using a guide for specific endings BUT ONLY AFTER your first playthrough. It would have been nice if the puzzle solutions were randomised, but it's not a deal breaker especially if you're only going to play through it once. Ib was a really enjoyable time overall! I ended up liking it a lot more than I would have initially thought. Give it a go if you're curious about it!

REVIEW #249
================================================================================
User: PertKhan
Steam ID: 76561198207026023
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 11.3 hrs on record
Date: Posted: July 29, 2022

Posted: July 29, 2022
																For ten years, I've been meaning to play this legendary title. Having been one of the big names during the time of the RPG Horror Golden Age, it was the talk of the internet alongside games like Mad Father and Witch House back in the day. I was so happy to see Ib get a remake for Steam, as I had been wanting Ib to join the Steam roster much like it's other fellow legendary titles I mentioned above. So, I bought Ib and FINALLY played it...it was amazing!I love these games for how creative they are. They just ooze raw creativity, you can tell the creator enjoyed making it. That makes me enjoy it even more! The concept was interesting, the characters lovable, and the game simple. This game was short naturally, around 2-3 hours tops. But for people that wish to see everything the game has? Get all collectibles? See every ending and get extra lore? Seems to be around 10+ hours. I'm at 10 hours at the time of writing this review, and only have a few endings left to see before I've seen every inch of the game.If you love story driven indie games fueled by pure skill and passion, you'll love Ib. It truly is a legendary classic as the people say. Highly recommend.

REVIEW #270
================================================================================
User: Edlinklover
Steam ID: 76561198078996258
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 9.8 hrs on record
Date: Posted: August 24, 2022

Posted: August 24, 2022
																I've loved this game for so long and have always wished for a way to financially support the creator somehow, and I'm so happy people finally can. This game genuinely changed my life and was the first horror game I've played and completed by myself. As for the remake, it retains most of the core game while improving and adding new character interactions and puzzles (no more math!) that are very welcome. I will say that I felt some of the scares had more impact in the original, but otherwise is a significant improvement to an already incredible game. This game is just very atmospheric in a way that sticks with you for years and its scares don't rely on blood and gore. Proper care is put into each painting and extra info about the museum to make it really feel like you're wandering through the gallery of an actual famous artist (even though he's completely fictional). Something I really appreciate about Ib is how accessible it makes horror to people who might otherwise be scared of it. As someone who loves horror games but usually can't play them myself, Ib gave me plenty of scares but it wasn't so terrifying that I couldn't progress. It's also about 2-3 hours long but it genuinely feels longer than that. If you want to see everything the game has to offer, it WILL be much longer than that. There is a story that helps make everything cohesive, but it doesn't get in the way of anything. Many RPG maker games tend to focus heavily on story with gameplay as an afterthought, but Ib's puzzles and atmosphere are well thought out and memorable. If you really like good puzzles and heavily atmospheric games, I'd definitely recommend this. Now I just want more accessible merch LOL

REVIEW #274
================================================================================
User: NathanVenture
Steam ID: 76561198837260029
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 30.1 hrs on record
Date: Posted: July 19, 2022

Posted: July 19, 2022
																I first heard of Ib when I was a young teen, and at the time I thought it was one of the greatest stories I'd ever seen. Now as a young adult having 100% completed the remake, I can say with certainty that Ib remains an excellent story-centric horror adventure that could both warm my hardened heart and keep me up at night with worry (thanks, Final Stage.) While the decision to switch from dark, messy sketches to brighter pixel art may be questionable as an aesthetic change, I enjoyed many of the other changes and new features like zooming in and the ability to talk to Garry on command.Talking to Garry itself is especially praiseworthy as there are multiple location/event sensitive lines in a majority of rooms in the game. For example, if you find the hider in the room of curtains on your first try, you can get a unique reaction from Garry for every other curtain if you backtrack there. That's a ton of optional dialogue that is incredibly easy to miss since not every player would be tempted to backtrack after finding Garry, and those who would backtrack would've also probably checked every curtain before moving on. While talking to Garry in this way is now tied to getting the game's good ending, it is only necessary to see 20 of the 200 or more new Garry lines to get the highest possible bond from doing so, leaving you free to not talk to him for long stretches without getting a less happy ending.The sheer attention to detail in Ib is commendable, and feels increasingly special as the AAA games industry slides further towards rushed releases, homogenized gameplay, superficial choices, live services and maximum monetization - with few exceptions.

REVIEW #300
================================================================================
User: Cave Johnson
Steam ID: 76561198025501070
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 2.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 19, 2022

Posted: May 19, 2022
																The original RPG Maker horror classic, redone in a higher screen resolution and new engine for it's tenth anniversary. If you're new here: Ib's brand of horror comes with a focus on puzzles, characterisation, and atmosphere. It's popularity partially comes from the fact that it was designed with genre newcomers in mind, so if you don't usually like horror this is a good place to start. There's no shock imagery, the scares are pretty restrained, the puzzles are fairer compared to other games of the era (lmao Ao Oni), and while some horrible things can happen to the cast if you're not careful they can usually be undone in another ending. ...Y'know. Usually.If you're familiar with the original: keep in mind that this version focuses on art/quality of life improvements, and doesn't contain much you haven't already seen. Some of the more obscure puzzles have been tweaked or outright replaced, chase sequences have been rebalanced to be more forgiving, and as far as I can tell there are no new areas or endings. It also adds the ability to talk to your companions at any time, which either gives you puzzle hints or fun dialog depending on what you're looking at.Bottom line: If you can't afford it, you can give this version a miss and play the original without missing any story beats or endings. If you can afford it, then this is a very solid remake that refines the clunkier parts of the original without messing with the parts people actually like.Either way, Ib is one of my favourite games of all time and worth checking out.

================================================================================
REVIEW #309
================================================================================
User: Aelyx
Steam ID: 76561199059847216
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 8.0 hrs on record
Date: Posted: March 6

Posted: March 6
Overall Rating ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÜStory ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÜGameplay ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÜGraphics ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖSoundtrack ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖSound Design ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÜDifficulty ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÜ‚òÜ‚òÜBug free ? ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖPC Requirements ‚òÖ‚òÜ‚òÜ‚òÜ‚òÜReplay Value ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÜ‚òÜStrongly Recommended - ‚úî‚úîAfter playing and reviewing The Witch House, I decided to continue my marathon of iconic independent RPG and what better way to continue it than to replay after so many years the silver medalist of the independent horror RPG podium: IB!Here you play the eponymous hero of the game, an 8 year-old girl named Ib who goes with her parents to a post-mortem exhibition of a very popular artist named Guertena. After looking at a strange painting, she finds herself in a parallel universe where Guertena's paintings and sculptures come to life. You must therefore survive in this sometimes surprising and sometimes frightening universe where you will meet different characters.So we start the game without being given too much information in the narration and this is already one of the strong points of this game : Most of the information is kept quiet. Unlike games where you are given all the keys to move forward and understand, where you can be disturbed by a scenario or elements that you don't like, Ib gives you the advantage of making your own story. The characters will give you some information, but it's up to you to interpret what you see. This kind of game has always had the merit of being considered incredibly original, and Ib is proudly part of it.Your goal will therefore be to get out of this museum with cursed paintings. You will never know what wants to harm you but you will want to escape. Not to mention that your red rose linked to your life, loses petals with each attack by these monsters and that you cannot defend yourself... But you will not be alone in your quest : A very effeminate and pleasant twenty-something man named Garry and a little blonde girl with blue eyes named Mary will accompany you.Having discovered and played IB for the very first time as a child, I had no idea that I was going to face a horror game. Because after all, with such 2D graphics, how can you be afraid of 6 moving pixels? Well yes, you will jump on your chair of surprise sometimes. The atmosphere of anguish is very present and very well transcribed.Speaking of atmosphere, the vibe given to the game is very special, having sometimes made me feel deeply uneasy. The game really succeeds in making you feel like you are in a gallery haunted by the creations of Guertena, a somewhat... special artist? And this through the very many paintings filling the gallery, the books telling us the story of these paintings, the puzzles related to them and the emotions they can make us transmit (it is quite special and incredible to make us feel emotions through these processes). Horror is also used intelligently to contribute to the atmosphere. The character of Ib, so small in the middle of the gallery, whose gloomy atmosphere is very well rendered, makes us, in spite of ourselves, tense up on our keyboard. The enigmatic side of the game, also, helps to perfect this gloomy atmosphere wonderfully: no indication, no arrows, no path to follow, no tutor or mentor who guides us during the game, nor any scenario indications. This disturbing universe will lead you to be curious and never get tired.For the gameplay : it's flawless for me. You should know that the vast majority of the gameplay is based on exploration and puzzles: The puzzles in the game are very interesting, tough but not impossible, allowing you to solve them while feeling proud of having accomplished them, very few of them rely on randomness not allowing you to go random and hope that it works.The exploration is also good, you have to explore a lot to continue the game but that the exploration is not restrictive, that the game makes you want to explore, thanks to its secrets, its many paintings etc... Bonus, to support how good its gameplay is: when you have to restart the game to do another ending, it does not stop you, it is quite easy to start again. Because my god it is annoying when you can not solve a puzzle that you already know because you had to do THIS action first because otherwise the variable does not work (sorry it is a bit technical but that is how Rpg Maker works, the program in which Ib was made), Ib very rarely has these problems and it is really pleasant to be able to redo it easily to explore all the endings. The aesthetics of the game are magnificent and original. At first terrified, we discover and delight in every detail of the story, which will gradually reveal the secrets of the world in which Ib is taken. The fact that the game is (relatively) short is ultimately an advantage when you want to replay the game to get another ending, because the outcomes are multiple. The scenario is very rich and has many twists and turns. But what you should remember the most is that you will be entitled to about ten different endings depending on the choices you make. So replay the game if the ending you got doesn't satisfy you, you will discover a new facet of the exhibition and new answers to your questions.Ib is a game that moved me a lot when I was younger, a game that changed my vision of what a good video game is. A game that showed me that you don't have to play a Light Novel to have a good story, that you don't have to have good graphics to have an incredible atmosphere, that you don't have to make a love story to make a relationship between two characters very touching. The story has no major flaws, nor did I see any huge inconsistencies, which puts us even more into the game. The story is full of mysteries that are complemented by different special events triggered by different fairly logical sequences of actions and/or with the endings. We can therefore make connections on our own, guesses about the sequel or the mysteries, etc... which is really nice and makes us "enter" the universe of IB. To come back to the different endings of Ib: they are also very good, leaving us with no bitter taste after having done them all, they are also accessible quite logically, so we can discover them without having really followed a guide but simply by our simple spirit of deduction (I personally had to look at a guide to do only two of them, and my god these endings are hard to achieve even with a guide which I find quite negative: having to talk 25 times to a character specifically at a time to unlock an ending. I say no: it is neither logical, nor intuitive, nor fun. Fortunately the excellent ending "A Painting Demise" makes up for these dozens of painful failures.) I would like to add that the option in the menu to be able to visit the real exhibition is just so great and satisfying: Finishing the different endings and discovering each work of the game and its titles will fill the real exhibition and we will also be able to find the important characters of the game to chat with them. It's a small bonus, very satisfying for any collector (even more so when you know that you have to finish completing the exhibition to get the game's only achievement on Steam).In short, Ib is an excellent game developed by a single person, which still beats three quarters of current AAA games. This is the perfect example of what is good in a horror/indie horror rpg and when I was younger, it made me discover a whole section of a genre of games that I did not know, the Indie Horror type Rpg Maker and I am very happy to have discovered it. It is illustrated by an excellent atmosphere, excellent gameplay and a very good story. Ib is striking, surprising, pleasant and will leave you with a very good memory. This game personally marked me, it touched me deeply, it will remain engraved in my memory like a thorn in my heart.

REVIEW #370
================================================================================
User: The People's Brickster
Steam ID: 76561198073015110
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 2.9 hrs on record
Date: Posted: January 23

Posted: January 23
																I wish Steam had a neutral button. I don't want to give it a "not recommended" but I wouldn't particularly recommend it unless you've played the original and are a superfan.To put it bluntly: despite being made for an improved engine, it feels less polished than the original game. Some of the new touches are cute, like the stool from the yellow area, or the newspaper girl in the white area, but other changes feel weaker than the original puzzles. For what it's worth, I think some of it is to reduce difficulty for new players, which is fine.I think the real issue comes with the visuals. Some of the new sprites are beautiful. Some of the new portraits are stiff as hell. Ib's dad looks very weird, though I'll admit that no one would probably notice unless they played the original game as much as I did. The new lighting is acceptable in the gallery, but it looks downright terrible in the sketchbook; the original sketchbook area is neon crayon art, that's the point. The new lighting system does not match the design at all. It should be bright, it should clash.Despite everything, I think I'm marking this as recommended. I still had fun, it's still the game I knew and loved, even if I do think the original version is still better. I appreciate all of the new dialogue between the characters a lot, even if it is just padding. This is effectively a donation button for fans of the original game, with a cute little remake attached.

REVIEW #410
================================================================================
User: WowItsBow
Steam ID: 76561198082336140
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 2.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: April 28, 2023

Posted: April 28, 2023
																Ib is a psychological horror masterpiece set in an art museum that tells so much within its short 2 hour runtime. Despite being a short game, Ib poses many complex themes and ideas that it gives most major games a run for their money at showing them how to create immersive worlds and levels without getting dragged out. The setting of exploring an alternative world of the museum where all of the artworks and statues are the main enemies is such a amazing unique concept that is incredibly engaging to play through. The music is fantastic and sets the eerie atmosphere, and loud well timed sound effects shatter the silence when exploring the map. Ib plays with themes of psychosis and alternating perspectives, combining these two things delivers a one of a kind horror experience that is perfectly brought to life in this remaster, one of the better remasters ever released. The characters are memorable, the setting is stylish and the whole experience is unforgettable. 9/10.

This remake is great, it adds so much more depth to the original museum by adding more rooms and puzzles to explore. My only flaw upon this remake is the removal of Mary's song "Puppet". Puppet was replaced with a new song and I don't understand why. The new song is good but in my personal opinion will never be as iconic and haunting the original is. Other than that one flaw, I really enjoyed replaying Ib. It doesn't deserve to be as underrated as it is, and is in my personal opinion an RPG maker classic.

The conceit of collecting all the paintings in the True Guertena Exhibit is also kind of addictive and gives you lots of opportunities to reexperience the game. The characters are all likeable, and also the walkthroughs are well-documented in the game's Steam guides section so you won't get hopelessly lost.Definitely try Ib. It's a game that's gotten something like a million downloads in Japan, but it's not very well-known to Anglophones, and that's a shame.

I adore this game. The creator is a genius who speaks uncensored to the essence of my soul. This game is criminally underrated, but my hope is that a Steam release will enlightened many more to the true value of this game. My warmest gratitude to Kouri. Please know how loved your masterpiece truly is.

REVIEW #472
================================================================================
User: jnarag2112
Steam ID: 76561199036200999
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.1 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 20, 2022

Posted: May 20, 2022
																Ib is a fantastic game. The music, the art, the premise, it's all brilliantly executed with charm.Having first played it in 2012/2013, I can say that the remake feels much more polished and feels like there's more incentive to explore than before. There's slight differences to some of the puzzles, but not an overwhelming difference, and they can be quite fun to solve. The sprites are also different, and look much more clearer than before, along with the dialogue for the characters being fantastically written and not too unrealistic. The English translation is very good and coherent! The zoom in tool, although I didn't find much real use for it, was also a very nice addition, especially for looking at the paintings closer.It's a shame the rose in the top left (representing Ib's health) in the original wasn't kept, now using a different picture, and I preferred some of the art for sprites in the original. I was also hoping that there would be at least another new ending or more backstory explored here, but I'd still recommend trying this one out alongside the original.All in all, a brilliant game that anyone can get into, and worth checking out, even if you've played the original before.

REVIEW #481
================================================================================
User: Wendy's
Steam ID: 76561198260462214
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 6.4 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 18, 2022

Posted: May 18, 2022
																The moment I saw Ib appear on Steam, I paid the $12 and played through everything in 1 session till I 100% the entire game. Perhaps this is because I'm biased, but Ib and The Witch's House were my 2 favorites back in 2013-2015. I had no idea Ib had a remake until the day I wrote this review.That being said, I can tell you with absolute certainty that this version of Ib is the better version. They changed the art style significantly, and Ib looks a lot more fleshed out as well as all the other characters. The dialogue is mostly the same, with some extra things thrown in here and there for touch-ups.They also changed some of the puzzles for the betterment of game design which is a MASSIVE plus. They did away with a lot of the "number" related puzzles (One example is the green room that once involved figuring out 3 numbers to multiple and add together to get the code to a door, now has been completely reworked so that you don't have to do that). Also, the new options of being able to talk to side characters at any point, as well as the new Zoom In/Zoom Out feature is absolutely incredible. They really outdid themselves this time by going above and beyond with the rework.As for criticism, I think this game can get quite repetitive if you're trying to strive for multiple endings. Ib has lots of different endings, and variations of those endings, but it's usually really tedious to get them. This has to do with the fact that the system they use to determine your ending usually requires analyzing decisions you've made pretty early in the game, as well as mid-way. So it can get quite hectic hopping around between saves, and replaying the same puzzles over and over again without an option to skip them, just for the sake of trying different choices. The True Gallery returns to Ib, and while there is one thing I won't necessarily spoil, I will say there are some "collectibles" that are very infuriating to locate without the walk through back on the original homepage at vpg translations. Some collectibles are even locked away without any way to backtrack and grab them. (Especially one in the blue room and brown room). Overall though, still absolutely love Ib, and I'm so happy to see it got a remake along with all of its other rpg horror cousins. Very much worth while for new players and old players alike!

Date: Posted: September 7, 2022

Posted: September 7, 2022
																A game that I wholeheartedly adore. Ib is an RPGMaker horror game that I feel stands out from its peers like Mad Father and The Witch's House. A lot of RPGMaker horror games have very similar vibes and tropes, giving them while often times distinct feels, nonetheless samey ones. Ib is a noticeable departure from many of those tropes, with a unique visual theme and tone. It feels like a strange and creepy yet enjoyable daydream where when you snap out of it at the end you're still left with mysteries to turn over and characters to remember. It's charming, it's creepy, it's clever, it's amazing.

REVIEW #540
================================================================================
User: Cat
Steam ID: 76561198071302392
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 14.0 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 19, 2022

Posted: May 19, 2022
																I didn't know about this remake until I stumbled on a random announcement on twitter about an English patch that just came out for it. I don't think I've purchased a game so quickly before.A remake of one of the classic staples of the Japanese RPG Maker Horror line up. But not in a bad way. Ib has been my favorite of this line for a very long time and this remake did not disappoint. The art and graphics are updated, most of the music is the same and some new features have been added! What surprised, yet delighted me was that there were new puzzles for old fans to try out. Some puzzles have been replaced, removed, added or revamped but not in a bad way. It keeps things interesting for older fans. A lot of room layouts have changed quite a bit as well.Everything has a nice glow up graphically and I really enjoy the 'talk to your partner' button. They have something new to say in every room and sometimes multiple things to say in a room depending on where you stand or what you've done in said room. It's a really nice touch.If I had any complaints, it would be the new health meter and the change in Mary's theme. I did like the original health meter and watching your rose lose petals instead of the new means where thorns disappear and the flower fades in color. But that's -hardly- a complaint and I'm kind of reaching when I call that a complaint. It is a shame Mary's theme changed as I much prefer the original, however I'm sure there's a reason for this. (Whether it be due to copyright or what may you)The extra bit of 'finding' the paintings and the requirements to consider them 'found' is a pretty neat addition and you may have to play through the game a couple of times to get them all as some depend on how you let an event play out. I thought I had gotten all of the base game paintings only to find that I missed two and one was due to how I let a event go.I can't recommend Ib enough. Both the original and this version. Considering the original game recently turned 10 years old, its a good time for this game to appear! Remakes don't always live up to the original. But this one certainly does and more.

This game I would very much describe as a comfort game as weird as that sounds because in a way it was "baby's first horror game(s)". I will continue to cherish Ib and its characters for a long time. I will never forget the first time I achieved the true ending way back when and I won't forget it now. This game is a treasure and I highly recommend it to those of you who are curious about it/have already known about RPGMaker horror games.
