REVIEW #553
================================================================================
User: SammiSafetypin
Steam ID: 76561198263722068
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 4.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 25, 2022

Posted: May 25, 2022
																I first got into Ib way back when, when I was just a 11 year old running around the internet. I came across a bunch of RPGMaker-based horror games, and while I loved many, Ib is the one that stuck out in my mind for a long, long time. The characters stand out very strongly despite the shortness of the game, and all manage to shine in their own ways, and the aesthetics stuck with me as well-- it was my first exposure to a horror game, leading me further and further into the genre. I said many times it was my favorite game of all time. So of course I had high expectations for the remake, and kouri absolutely, 200% delivered. Even just opening the title screen and hearing the music made me feel like I was home. The visuals are amazing-- they're a direct upgrade to the original game's graphics (including fixing text readability issues), without sacrificing aesthetic or the heart of a classic RPGMaker game. In a gaming climate where a lot of games will clamor to have the new best, most glimmering, most advanced never-before-seen graphics advancements in the world, that classic RPGMaker vibe that doesn't fight to add every pore to its graphics imaginable is a breath of fresh air. It's pretty, charming, and the pixel art is absolutely gorgeous-- I found myself often using the zoom function just to take in the quality of some of the work.The only thing I can possibly criticize here is that I feel the game can hold your hand a little too much with its puzzles sometimes. It may just be the brain of someone who's been obsessed with this game for years, but I do feel sometimes the game did a little too much wink-wink nudge-nudge. Even so, that's preferable to no direction at all, and it's really just a minor gripe.I know it's easy to be blinded by nostalgia because of my fondness for this game. But doing my absolute best to be objective, Ib is still a haunting game with a story that has stood the test of time, and I think even if this is your absolute first time even learning it exists, you'll have a terribly great time in Guertena's gallery.I'm gonna talk about spoilers past this, but let it be known that even if you can only read this far-- Ib is 100% worth your time and money. It's a great, atmospheric little game perfect for even those new to the horror genre, while still being deeply unsettling. Great characters, great environment, great story, 10/10 any story with haunted art still makes me go crazy in a good way.[Story spoilers below this point.]The story is just how I remember it, seeming pretty directly lifted. Which is no problem at all, because Ib has always had a great story and it maintains here. A chilling atmosphere without needing to be over-the-top, the sense of deep, permeating unease drags you in, the idea that anything in the gallery could reach out for you at any time. The fact that there's only very occasional chases adds to this, making you just high-strung enough without letting you get too used to it. Chases are generally simple but still stressful-- the escape from the Toy Box will always make my heart pound. Garry is an incredibly charming, sweet character, reliable as the only adult but obviously still stressed and nervous. Ib is a silent protagonist, but it's made clear that she is still a young girl cracking under the pressure. Their reactions to the gallery seem very real, adding further to the uncanny valley of just how unsettling this place really would be for someone. And of course, Mary remains one of my favorite antagonists in any game -- a young child who you can't fully blame for her actions, likely not understanding human morality from being raised in the fabricated world, that just wants to be real, but the only option is to do something terrible. It makes her as scary as she is sympathetic, and I think that's a strength of Ib. The tragedy of how the gallery works, of this inherent imbalance where someone must be trapped forever or even die, makes it all the sadder. I want Mary to be happy, wanting to escape isn't a bad wish and the circumstances aren't her fault, but I don't want Ib or Garry to die in the fabricated world either. It's just people at the whims of the gallery, and that's what makes it so compelling. Not to mention how charming Mary is, just as much as the other two -- yes Mary you DO look so cute in your scarf.The new puzzles are very fun, and I think the ones that were replaced from the original game make sense -- for example, replacing the equation in the yellow area with the tree windup keys feels a lot more artsy and true to the gallery than doing math. The teacup puzzle was fun and made me remember I'm bad at sliding puzzles, and I'm obsessed with that cat thing in the gray area. Also, oh my god the last chase in the grey area is so much more stressful!! I say that positively!! The changes to the puzzles in that area as well as the insanely stressful chase are top-tier, and I love that the nightmare sequence is so much more horrifying and now has control. Paradoxically, being able to move in that only makes me feel even less in control-- it's amazing!I could go on forever, really, I could, about the new graphics, new puzzles, how charming all of the new Garry and Mary dialogue is (and the time it must have taken to add all of it!), the cute new talksprites and how painful the one of Mary starting to burn is... and all of the music, god I could genuinely just gush forever. Also, did the doll room get its timer shortened or is it just me? Scared the ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• out of me. All in all, Ib remains my favorite game of all time. Play it now.

																I want to start this review by saying that I did not want to play this game. I'm serious! The only reason I did was as a part of a deal between me and a friend. I literally went into this game with the lowest expectations possible (not to say that I thought the game was going to be bad, just that I wouldn't enjoy it).And despite that... it's pretty solid! I played the original game and it itself was nice. The atmosphere was appropriately spooky, the characters were cute, and the story was fairly compelling, at times. This remake (which was gifted to me by aforementioned friend) only improves on the strengths of the original, while adding replayability atop the base game's normal endings by adding collectible paintings that you can view in your very own art galleria. If my impressions of the game, as someone who doesn't really play RPGs, was at least lukewarm, I can only imagine how much someone who does enjoy RPGs would like this remake. Highly recommend to anyone who does.

REVIEW #620
================================================================================
User: Haleskull217
Steam ID: 76561199071007453
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 10.4 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 30, 2022

Posted: June 30, 2022
																I was really excited for the Ib remake to come out, since the original is a favorite of mine. I'm very happy to say this is a great remake and that it actually improves upon the original game.I absolutely love the new conversation system and how it allows for even more dialogue/interaction with the characters. Additionally, I was pleasantly surprised by just how much extra dialogue there was. It may seem like a small thing, but it gives the characters more depth and makes them even more interesting/likeable (and this is coming from a person who already loved Garry in the original).The art has also been touched up and looks even better than before. These improvements are especially noticeable in the character sprites and CGs. For the remake, the puzzles were reworked and made to be a bit easier as well. Some fans of the original might have a problem with this, but I thought it was fine. Because of these changes the puzzles have a better flow to them and are suitable for players of all skill levels. Overall, I absolutely loved the Ib remake and would highly recommend it. Whether you've played the original or not, I think the remake is definitely worth giving a try. I'd go so far as to say the Ib remake is the best way to experience an already fantastic game.

================================================================================
REVIEW #656
================================================================================
User: YuuyaKZMI
Steam ID: 76561198073578393
Recommendation: Negative
Hours Played: 7.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: April 3

Posted: April 3
Product received for free
																This game is a remake of the original Ib from 2012.But as someone who has been a fan of it since years before it was made, I would say this is an Ib remake for Ib fans. If this is your first time playing or seeing Ib, don't buy this, and go play the original. It's free. The primary reason I say that is because the most integral part of the game was butchered.The aesthetic.Visual atmosphere is EVERYTHING in Ib. Without spoiling anything, it was built with darker colors and deeper shading in mind. The remake favors a more bright, colorful and retro aesthetic; which kills a lot of moments where the original's art direction would have been better for a first experience. The characters were also butchered with the brighter coloring, and it's so much less fluid. They come out flat, and some of them look straight up robotic.I'm not saying the art style is bad, but it doesn't work for the type of game Ib is, which relies heavily on visual direction. If you're a newcomer, then play the original first. This is an Ib remake for long-time Ib fans who already have experienced the original game.

REVIEW #694
================================================================================
User: Jobko
Steam ID: 76561198069166359
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.2 hrs on record
Date: Posted: February 7, 2024

Posted: February 7, 2024
																Every little detail matters. Ib is a game with multiple endings, requiring multiple playthroughs. Through each playthrough you‚Äôll have to play differently, and for 100% completion almost every interaction matters. This makes Ib a memorable experience, with every area, puzzle, painting, character, and dialogue sequence being ingrained in your brain. This level of careful attention to detail, and overall quality of that detail, makes Ib one of the best RPG Maker games to date. The story itself is unique, and multi-layered, with repeated playthroughs containing details you‚Äôd miss on first glance. The game is also rather short, not feeling like a burden to repeat. The endings and extra interactions/dialogue sequences you‚Äôll experience enhance your overall connection to the games characters and story. As someone who came into this with no expectations or prior knowledge, I‚Äôm ecstatic. Goosebumps covered me upon experiencing the true ending, overwhelmed with joy due to the trials needed to unlock it. While the gameplay is simple, given it‚Äôs a RPG Maker game, Ib manages to explore various different puzzles, each unique, culminating to the completion of each area. These get progressively more challenging, with some even requiring the use of multiple characters to finish.The games True Guertena Exhibit is the icing on top, as you explore an exhibit featuring all the games art work, music, and endings, requiring 100% completion to finish. Also the bonus content you unlock on second playthrough feels like a sizeable expansion to the games content/story, so you have more to look forward to outside of whatever ending you‚Äôre going for. Ib is one of those games that feels ‚Äúperfect‚Äù, with no real issues outside of personal taste or nitpicks. An indie classic that needs to be experienced.

REVIEW #719

User: korvakoiraa
Steam ID: 76561199804693957
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 6.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: November 4

Posted: November 4
																IB is one of the most recognizable RPGmaker games of all time for good reason. The 3 characters are fleshed out in such a short amount of time, on top of having a beautiful story and fun gameplay. The visuals are striking, it uses the setting of an art gallery to it's fullest, and is genuinely so visually striking while still staying true to the pixel art RPGmaker style.A normal playthrough takes anywhere from 2-3~ hours depending, which given the price tag of the game is a bit steep. But the experience is well worth it and a must play for any RPGmaker fan. The game sports only one achievement which takes replaying the game several times, it can get a bit tedious at times but once you've played through the game once you realize how short it actually is. It took me only 6 and a half hours to 100% IB and see every ending and it was well worth it. Garry is the best, and the true ending is so touching... you have to play this game it's iconic. It's IB.

REVIEW #760
================================================================================
User: FaeBee
Steam ID: 76561198314807970
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.1 hrs on record
Date: Posted: July 8

Posted: July 8
An RPG maker puzzle classic; I'd absolutely watch an anime if it got oneGreat game, not too long, but plenty of bonus content for those who want to get more out of this game, my only real criticism is some cutscenes could do with a skip option after you've seen it once or twice, since multiple playthroughs is required to fill the gallery (the only achievement this game has).I think this game could do with more achievements, even if all of them are just ones you'd unlock on your way to getting the only achievement the game has, but I don't think it's really the focus of the game, it doesn't detract by only having 1 achievement, it's just fun to have more to work for, or to have those little milestones along the way as you go for the main one.the music is great, and the art, which is important considering the entire game takes place in an art museum, I feel like there's some yume nikki influences here too which is always a plus, it's great as a fan of yume nikki to see where it's inspired other works, there's great atmosphere, the characters are alright although honestly I felt it could've perhaps done with a couple more, but there are benefits to a limited cast I suppose.I did notice a couple typos in my playthrough, but nothing that'd be an issue for understanding puzzles or anything, it's not going to ruin your experience with the game and they're pretty few and far between.I haven't played the original Ib so I don't know how it stacks up comparatively, or whether what this version adds is substantial enough to pay for, but I enjoyed it, I'll probably give the original free version a go since I enjoyed this one so much.also I want to add, at points the music made me reminiscent of some of the music in LiEat, so if you were a fan of this game's soundtrack perhaps you'd enjoy LiEat, although I realise this game's is a bit more atmospheric and tries to lean more into ambiguity and an eerie feeling, both are good but they both attempt to do different things, so it's not one to one the vibe is different between them despite the similarities, but nonetheless, maybe a good option if you enjoyed the music of Ib.Update: I've since played the original Ib and this one is betterIf you preferred the original, I totally get it, it goes more for atmosphere and claustrophobia, and yeah, this game does lose a bit of that, you have the option of a more zoomed in camera, but no one is gonna use it, and it's too zoomed in even if you did want to.The original Ib isn't as good in the ways of the art or the puzzles, not to say they're bad or anything, but this one just does it better in my eyes, there's a lot less room for misunderstanding with this version, the rough spots are fixed, and there are even points where this one gets the atmosphere better, for example the room full of paintings of a lady, the original just tries to unleash them all on you, and it's more annoying than tense, this version only releases a couple to keep you on your toes, and then there's 1 which is an actual threat during the chase sequence, there's less room for error, getting trapped by a dozen ladies in a painting, it's more straightforward, but just as -if not more- tense.If you preferred the original Ib, I totally get it, I think this version could do better at capturing the feeling of claustrophobia, or utilising darkness to elevate the atmosphere, but if you're going to tell me the original is the best way to experience Ib for any new player, you need to give them both a try again, and maybe get 2 different friends to try one and the other, have one start with the original, and one start with the remake, and hopefully then you'll get why this one is just a better and more well-rounded experience. Having a preference is fine, but you've gotta be realistic when it comes to player experience.

																I discovered Ib only this year through another game that had a collaboration with it. I liked the vibe of that collab, and it intrigued me enough to finally check out Ib for myself.As someone who hasn‚Äôt played many games of this style‚Äîaside from Undertale and a few others‚ÄîI found Ib to be unique and engaging in its own quiet, eerie way. At first, I felt that going through the entire in-game gallery and interacting with every painting was a bit tedious; there were moments when it even made my hand hurt. But the atmosphere, the vibe, and the overall experience outweighed the simplicity of the game‚Äôs controls.For me, the biggest highlight of Ib is the sense of exploration‚Äîand the tension of constantly being on edge, waiting to see what might happen next. I‚Äôve only played through the game once and got a good ending, but I know there are multiple endings and more content to discover in future playthroughs, which I‚Äôm looking forward to.I usually like going into games blind (aside from what I picked up through the collab), and I prefer figuring things out on my own before diving into the lore. One detail that really caught my attention (spoiler alert) was how both Ib and her mother resemble the mysterious women in Guertena‚Äôs paintings. It made me wonder if there‚Äôs any deeper meaning, or if it‚Äôs just a coincidence‚Äîbut that kind of open-endedness is part of the game‚Äôs charm.To sum it up: gameplay-wise, it‚Äôs simple, with some satisfyingly tricky puzzles along the way. Story-wise, it‚Äôs mysterious, atmospheric, and leaves room for personal interpretation. Definitely worth playing if you enjoy slow-burn storytelling, exploration, and eerie puzzles.

REVIEW #796
================================================================================
User: not not a box
Steam ID: 76561198016557161
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 2.4 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 13

Posted: May 13
																Very nice game from the classic RPGMaker era.Puzzles are mechanically simple (find correct key/item and use it on the correct spot), but there's a mysterious atmosphere that makes you always wonder "what's coming next".A few jumpscares, but most of the horror comes from the uneasy feeling the art gallery offers. It's still rather "light"; there are only a handful of "enemies" which can be avoided easily. There's a couple rooms that are really tense, and in which failing IS an option. Considering there are several endings, keep that in mind as you save your progress.Overall, scary ambiance, interesting visuals and puzzles, and a very short length (finished in 2.3 hours for the main story, I'd wager to see all the endings it'd take 3-4 hours more). So if you want a horror game you can finish in one sitting, and/or miss the good old RPGmaker style games, go for it!

Still the same experience, and not as long, but a very sweet weekend game. Now, please enjoy the game: Welcome to the World of Guertena.

REVIEW #869
================================================================================
User: Aloe
Steam ID: 76561199086390133
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 9.4 hrs on record
Date: Posted: November 2, 2024

Posted: November 2, 2024
																Ib is a very short and cute little game. one of the staples of the RPGhorror genre.you play as little 9-year old Ib (pronounced "Ebe" (probably meant to be Eve?? but Japan doesn't have the letter 'V' to it turned to "Ebe")) exploring a spooky little art gallery filled with not very friendly paintings and artworks. The puzzles you have to go through are fairly simple yet still fun to solve. soem can be pretty head-scratching too.the background music is eerie and sets-up the game's atmosphere nicely.the pixel art and character portraits are well-made and unique in it's own right. Though the game has "horror" as one the tags, it's really not that scary. But i don't really see that as a negative. it just means it's more accesible to folks who may not be all too fond of jumpscares (speaking of which, there're like, 2 jumpscares at best in this game. The horror mostly comes from the unsettling imagery depicted through it's simple pixel graphics.The story itself is very simple and cute. it has it's moments, some twists and turns, but overall i'd consider it pretty average amongst other 2D story-based pixel RPGs with hints of depression‚Ñ¢. I'd put the story to be on par with Mad Father, but sliiiiiiiightly lower. by a veeeeery small margin.idk how this game is priced in other countries but i'd definitely recommend picking it up when it's on sale.7.9/10 game very cute and simple.

																I've absolutely adored this game ever since I was a kid, and I CANNOT recommend this remake/remaster enough honestly.  While I do have a few tiny nitpicks (puppet being cut from the ost, the sketchbook feeling a bit emptier than the original, less chase sequences) they pale in comparison to just how great the game still is and all the QOL changes the remake has.  Absolutely love having the option to talk to Garry at any time, both for ending purposes and just to spend more time with him cuz he rocks.  The map in general had a massive facelift and it's definitely for the better, everything just flows WAY better than it did before and when comparing it to the original it shows.  I do think the sketchbook loses a bit of it's creepiness from this but it's far from a deal breaker in the grand scheme of things. Everything is streamlined while still remaining super interesting and keeping the charm of the original. There's so many other subtle but amazing changes that I adore, I really hope kouri ends up making another game some day because his style is absolutely amazing.

It took roughly 4 playthroughs for me without a guide, which pushed my play time more realistically to 12-15 hours or so? I would be extreeemely remiss not to mention the puzzles. Some puzzles were simplistic, easy, but had fun and unexpected resolutions which kept things fun. Other puzzles were creepy, or complex and made me feel engaged. In any case, exploration is rewarded, thought provoking puzzles keep it fun, and the narrative and music are pretty good - with the music being stand out. This remake of the original really delivers.

																I remember the original Ib. I was young and my sister found it and I didnt even play it until I watched her beat it like 3 times. I love Ib and the way they make her feel like a real child in this situation, Garry who is dumb, but kind doing anything he can to help Ib and Mary who I hated my first playthrough years ago I later liked the mosty cause even when you first meet her you can tell something is off and to see her loneliness especially with the new endings they added are just amazing.

REVIEW #934
================================================================================
User: Dr. Freakenstein
Steam ID: 76561198317117096
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 9.0 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 10, 2024

Posted: May 10, 2024
																I absolutely adore this game. I feel like it's an essential when getting into RPGmaker horror, alongside Corpse Party, and has been one of my favorite games since it came out. This was my first time playing the remake and I fell in love all over again. It's short and sweet and has great replayability since there's like several different endings. The soundtrack is iconic and I still listen to it to this day, Mary's Theme in particular has sat with me for years. It feels obvious to say the game feels interactive and lively when the main premise is about works of art trying to attack you, but I don't know how else to describe. I love the little details when you interact with the different pieces, the world of Ib definitely feels immersive. We only get to really know three characters, one of them being Ib who is the player character, but the personality both Garry and Mary have never get bored. Especially now that I am already I have a greater appreciation for Garry, who has always been a favorite character of mine. When I was younger, I always felt like he was cool and collected and knew exactly what he was doing, but playing this now, I realize that Garry was just as afraid and lost but kept on a brave face for Ib. Mary is a character I could talk about forever, but I am glad people sympathize with her more. I still have no clue how people despised this nine year old lol. The dialogue that comes from these two characters never gets old and, even though it might not be a lot dialogue, fleshes out them out a ton.Phenomenal game with phenomenal art, music, and characters. I can not recommend this game enough.

REVIEW #1031
================================================================================
User: Kain Klarden
Steam ID: 76561197989807190
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 4.8 hrs on record
Date: Posted: November 9, 2023

Posted: November 9, 2023
																While there is a numerous amount of horror themed adventure games made on RPG Maker, I‚Äôve never been fond of them usually. There have been some good examples here and there, but more often than not these games leaned too hard either in pure tasteless jumpscare territory or were simply too poorly written, relying on shock value or extreme themes. Due to that, I had no knowledge of Ib when it became an extremely popular free game back in the early 2010s and would have not paid attention to this 2022 updated (and no longer free) remake, if not for catching a few streams and videos on it. I am glad, however, that other people promoted this little gem and that I got to experience it for myself.Ib is a short horror themed adventure about a little girl who finds herself in a strange world where paintings come to life. And as it often happens with these RPG Maker based titles, it avoids the combat completely, instead focusing on avoiding enemies and traps and solving problems and puzzles. There are no special mechanics like stealth here, nor are the puzzles usually hard, so the game focuses mostly on just delivering a good story driven experience with lots of small and huge variations depending on how you play. Nicely enough, despite having quite a few different endings, the game isn‚Äôt really focused on this aspect as well and as far as ‚Äúunlocks‚Äù go, you only need to get a few of them, with the rest of endings only existing to provide an interesting reaction to your choices through the game and occasionally learn some little additional thing about the characters.Despite being a horror story and having some genuinely creepy ideas, the overall atmosphere of the game is more reminiscent of a darker folk tale or something one might expect from Through the Looking-Glass, and What Alice Found There. Which works really well and completely avoids the typical for these games issue of going for the gore or overdone tropes. Most of the puzzles in the game, I‚Äôd even say all of the ones in the main playthrough, are really fun too. While the extended playthrough, that is available upon replays, has some weaker moments, it‚Äôs still really fun. The visuals and the music are also really nice and the simplicity of style works really well for the game.I really enjoyed playing the game and my only real complaint is that due to the engine choice and overall style, the game runs in a rather small resolution by today‚Äôs standards and can become less comfortable to run in the future as resolutions increase. But it‚Äôs a rather minor thing and I could easily recommend anyone who likes horror themed adventure games to check Ib remake from 2022 out.

I'm happy with the super good ending I received, it's everything I hoped for.

REVIEW #1099
================================================================================
User: Grantholomeu
Steam ID: 76561198076311823
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 17.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: August 5, 2023

Posted: August 5, 2023
																Very charming and interesting little rpgmaker game. Story-wise, you are trapped in an odd art museum. The main focus of the gameplay is puzzles, often related to the artwork featured in the exhibitions you'll see. By completing puzzles, you hope to break out of the museum. Ib has a bit of a horror feel to it, but I wouldn't call is a horror game. It's more puzzle, narrative, and choices matter. If you are a completionist this may be a good game for you, because you are encouraged to collect all the artwork featured throughout the game. There are also a good number of different endings. Personally I got the few that were easy for me to get without replaying the whole game and called it, but if going back and seeing how every option affects the outcome of the story is your thing, you can do that. I was a bit confused as to why the puzzles and overall environment existed at all, but the game was fun and charming enough I can overlook that small qualm. It's a good game!

(I actually got the true ending first time around because I liked talking to Garry so much!)The gameplay itself was really fun. Ib really kept me on my toes! I ended up replaying the game a LOT of times..I definitely recommend it!!

REVIEW #1128
================================================================================
User: Roman
Steam ID: 76561198035632391
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 10.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 10, 2023

Posted: June 10, 2023
																This was a cute, yet creepy adventure.  There is no combat.  Occasionally, you'll need to avoid enemies.  Lots of puzzle solving, lots of collecting.The story is pretty interesting and actually gives the game a lot of replay value.  You cannot 100% the game without playing it a few times.  Luckily, you can skip any dialogue, but not scripted animations.  Lots of secrets that contribute to the player's understanding of what's happening.  Still, even if you complete and collect everything, it's up to you to mentally figure out what the deal is.Certain decisions affect the outcome of the game, while others merely affect what others say or how things behave or look.  There is a certain character whose fate depends on your decisions, as well as how good your relationship is with them.  The progress of these items is not shown, but is otherwise hinted at with different actions or dialogue.  It's a little complex, but nothing a guide wouldn't help with, should you wish to use one.Ultimately, this is a great game for completionists and those who are fans of creepy retro visuals and art-based themes.

REVIEW #1161
================================================================================
User: Xelester

Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 5.2 hrs on record
Date: Posted: April 2, 2023

Posted: April 2, 2023
																12/10Timeless Classic RPG maker horror game. Ib was one of my first experiences with RPG maker horror, and it left a great impression on me. The game is typical maker fashion, with added horror elements. Ib has a lot of puzzles that are easy to solve if u just pay attention. It has multiple endings, with only 3 being "main" endings? The characters are Ib, Gary and Mary. These 3 have been around for like 10 years now. This remake adds a bunch of new things which I didn't expect, new sprites, new levels, redesigneed rooms etc. Kouri even added a button to speak with your party members, which is even more dialogue + lore. The "horror" aspect of Ib remains as it was 10 years ago, it's not scary for me, this is true even now. But what drew me in was the story itself. Emotional and unique. Overall very good remake, hopefully more people are exposed to Ib.

REVIEW #1167
================================================================================
User: Chito
Steam ID: 76561198356672307
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 13.0 hrs on record
Date: Posted: March 26, 2023

Posted: March 26, 2023
																Ib is the first real horror game I've had growing up and my favorite of all time. The original game held a special place in my heart and when it came to recommending new people into horror, I would always recommend this game first. Everything in it was brilliant at the time and breathtaking as a child, the puzzles, the horror, being on edge, the hints, characters, atmosphere, everything was so unique compared to other horror games. It was more of a puzzle game to be fair and dived into it's story and character development more than it's horror element but that's what also made the moments where there where horror hit and hit hard. I'll never forget the moment where I was alone as Gary and meet that stupid doll, the moment where I was alone with Mary but still felt mistrust against her before I knew of her true nature, and lastly when being thrown into that toy box and trying to escape for the first time. All these moments are deep in my memory and will stay there. Though the one thing that really made me stay in this game other than the horror aspects and the puzzles, was Gary and Ib. I've never before cared much for a pixel that much, Each interaction, each moment together, and finally the end where Gary remembers Ib broke me to where I cried tears of joy to see that he remembers everything they went to. i could never forget all the times I was scared but I could never forget the times where his beautiful Guitar calmed me in these moments, to give me strength to carry on.Now, does this extent into the remake? Yes but also no. I enjoyed the Remake and I spent 12+ hours getting all 150 artworks without looking online(or trying to). I loved more interactions with Gary, I loved the new visuals, and New Puzzles. Though I wish there was more. Once I was done with the game I felt accomplished yet still not whole... like there needed to be more added to call this a remake. It also didn't help that some of the puzzles where removed to make the game easier, which I thought was taking away from the original. Overall, the only complaint I have is that I wish that there was more in this game. Then again, I had that same complaint in the original but this is a remake... it desires more. Perhaps a sequel? Though I doubt there will be one. Perhaps do the same with Mad father or Witches house and have a harder difficulty in the game which adds a secret ending or a new room, that would honestly help but that is up to the creator. P.S.If you're the creator of this beautiful Remake. Thank you for bringing me back to my childhood, back to simpler times, and making it overall feel like a brand new experience. Even though I wish there was more as stated before, this is still a damn fantastic remake that I'd recommend anyone. This will always be apart of my Memories.

																AaaaaaaaaaThis game will always hold a special place in my heart. Another part is the doll room which in the original I could consistently find the key but in this version I feel like I fail more often than not.In any case, overall I still highly enjoy and will fondly remember the game and I'd recommend it to anyone regardless of their genre preference. Alas, I again still wish to see more of the characters but I'm still grateful for a loving remake after ten years.

Anything beyond that gets kind of repetitive since very little changes in most of your choices until the end, you're better off watching a video of the endings you didn't get.Also, if you want to collect all the paintings make sure that you don't kill Garry after your first playthrough, since you need him to read out the titles that Ib doesn't understand.

REVIEW #1184
================================================================================
User: TheEpicPancake
Steam ID: 76561198056178083
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 2.4 hrs on record
Date: Posted: March 13, 2023

Posted: March 13, 2023
																A classic, and for good reason! It remains spooky and charming even all these years later, and the puzzles are a good time too! The only problem is that I beat it pretty dang quickly, so it's a bit of a hard sell for 12 dollars if you're focused on a time:money ratio. That being said, I've watched playthroughs of the game in the past, meaning the puzzles were quicker than average, and there does seem to be a degree of replay value here. I know there are variations to the endings, and it seems like there's some extra content after beating the game. I'm gonna leave it for another time, though. Overall, I'd highly recommend it if you're wanting for an experience that sticks with you despite a short runtime. If it's on sale, definitely go for it. As I said initially, it's highly regarded for a reason, and it's still worth your time if you haven't been spoiled on it.

REVIEW #1269
================================================================================
User: Odran
Steam ID: 76561198090798543
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: November 22, 2022

Posted: November 22, 2022
																One of the best rpg maker games, is up there with the likes of "The Witch's House", "Yume Nikki", "Mad Father", "Misao", etc.The thing that separates this game from the rest is, that it actually has a good story that poses a very simple philosophical tesis, wich is "the world is a percieved world". Each character has their own interpretation of the world, and they percive it through their own posibilities, their own background and knowledge of the world.For example, Ib doesn't know many words, so her perception and knowledge of this world is very limited, and so will be yours looking it throug her eyes. It also has a commentary in Barthe's Death of the author, the "main villain" of the story being a painting and all, invites us to think the art as more than what an author can concive. This also connects with the world as a perception on the self, one then learns more about themself by the way they percieve things, and every character even the villain is in a journey of selfknowldege.The puzzles are also quite fun, even more so the new ones, the new area is fine if a little short, and the special room is one of the greatest additions to this game. It improves significantly upon the original, but it also censores some aspects, like the imagery of death and suicide in the final area, wich is a minor complain. I recommend this version to old fans of the original and newcomers, it is a great and thought provoking experience.

You also have to make the right choices of course- Other then this my play through's were fun and nostalgic.In all I was super happy with this remake and seeing one of my childhood favourite games getting some love made me really happy.

================================================================================
REVIEW #1360
================================================================================
User: KuriChestnut
Steam ID: 76561198209318897
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 13.2 hrs on record
Date: Posted: July 13, 2022

Posted: July 13, 2022
																If I had to summarize my feelings for this game, Ib could be described as a horror rpg that is unique and is personally one of my favorite indie games to play. You take on the role of a girl named Ib, whom visits an art exhibition by the artist Guertena with her parents. It's not long after wandering into the gallery alone that Ib enters into another world and must pass multiple puzzles and countless killer artworks to escape. GraphicsFrom the beginning, Ib's graphics are absolutely stunning, with the game feeling very artsy yet having a touch of horror as the game's theme and genre suggests. Being a remake of the original game released in 2012, all of the graphics have been updated, including a major revamp of the character busts, the option to zoom into the game, and some of the obstacles/layout having been changed. Despite this, the game retains the aesthetic of the original in contrast to other remakes such as The Witch's House and Mad Father, which helps it give off the same feel as it's predecessor.MusicThere's not much to say about Ib's ost other than it is the same from the original. That being said, each song fits well with where you are in the game and it's cutscenes.Multiple ChoicesOne of the best thing about Ib are the choices you can make throughout the game that can lead to different endings. What makes Ib unique in this regard is rather than solely making choices to a certain ending, interaction with characters and the environment is also a big factor in what ending you get. This not only helps you get invested in getting to know the characters more and analyze your surroundings, but it is also something that helps Ib stand out as most games with multiple endings I feel only focus on doing a certain action or choice rather than taking advantage of the game itself. It really shows the potential of what doing or not doing can really have on a game.In conclusion, playing Ib was a fun experience that while lasting only a few hours, it really shows how much a single developer is capable of doing and how enjoyable a game can be despite it's length. Would definitely recommend to horror game fans and for people looking for something in the horror genre yet not too scary to make you jump out of your boots!

REVIEW #1377
================================================================================
User: Pwushie
Steam ID: 76561198384211710
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.2 hrs on record
Date: Posted: July 1, 2022

Posted: July 1, 2022
																Ib is an absolutely excellent game. This remake touches up quite a bit of the game from the original and includes new features, including the ability to talk to your current party members. There is a surprising amount of new dialog for this feature as well. The puzzles aren't too challenging and if you've played other games made in RPG Maker you will not have too much trouble. The most notable part of Ib is it's story, which is the primary reason this game has stuck in my head for so long. The story covers many themes, including isolation, the power of fiction, and the impact of an artist's legacy and uses these themes excellently. If you remember watching videos of or playing the freeware version back in 2012, I would absolutely recommend picking this up, you may be surprised by what you find.

REVIEW #1378

Posted: June 29, 2022
																I bought this game for the nostalgia. Ib is a very important game to me and a part of my childhood. This "Remake" improves the in-game sprite and puzzles. The translation is better compared to the old translation by vgperson, now he has improved it. Garry's manner of speech is more accurate compared to the old one which has been lost by translation. My only complains are the change of the art style in the character profile and CG, the older version had a more darker tone which is the kind of style I find more fitting with the haunted art gallery setting. The only times I feel threatened, in the game were the Woman in Grey and the Doll Room. The other creatures in the gallery are very slow compared to the original. This game is a classic with a very much alive fanbase and has stood the test of time. I highly recommend buying this game.

REVIEW #1399
================================================================================
User: lawyer_enjoyer
Steam ID: 76561199280297828
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 6.7 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 19, 2022

Posted: June 19, 2022
																Ib is yet more evidence that video games are a fantastic medium for storytelling. If you are looking for a horror game, you can find far scarier games, and admittedly, if you're looking for a good story-focused game, you could find better. But what makes this game good is the big picture. This game is a unique combination of things. It's eerie yet adorable. It's deep in it's own way, yet doesn't come off as pretentious. It's creepy, but not lonely. It has a small, yet lovable and memorable cast. For these reasons, I say that this is a fantastic "gateway horror game", for someone who is too scared to play things like Resident Evil or Silent Hill. The whole "RPG Maker Horror" genre can be considered great gateway horror games, but Ib in particular has something special about it. Unlike many horror games, RPG or otherwise, this game never kills you unfairly, and is really easy to boot. This was the very first horror game I ever finished, several years ago. This remake doesn't change a whole lot (although area layouts are different) but it gave me a reason to play through this great game again.

																Ib is a wonderful game, and this remaster retains just about all of the charm and spirit the original freeware version had. The game has been changed in a few ways, for example, some of the puzzles have been changed to be less annoying to solve. A change I don't really understand is why they changed Mary's theme. In the original, Mary's theme was probably one of the most iconic songs in the game, and the new version just feels bland and uninspired. That's the only thing I have against this version, everything else stays true to the original, and I can't recommend it enough. I haven't seen any post-game content yet, but I am hoping that it still stays true to the original.

REVIEW #1405
================================================================================
User: Sapien36
Steam ID: 76561198113048932
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 17, 2022

Posted: June 17, 2022
																The original Ib released in 2012 was my first introduction to the RPG horror genre. Before this remaster was released, I must have played the original like 6 or so times out of both nostalgia and a genuine love for the story, characters, and art. This is the game that inspired me to learn more about (and eventually dabble in) game making, and Kouri's blog gave me some of my first resources to start that progress. I think it goes without saying at this point, but I was more than excited to see that a remake was on the way!If I'm being honest, I was a little worried that the major hype I had going in would make my expectations a little high- but *wow* was I wrong! The remake is a perfect blend of old and new, containing not only a polished new look but refreshing puzzles to keep it interesting for returning players. Oh, and I can't forget to mention my favorite non-spoiler part of the remake, the loads of new dialogue added to every single area of the game- really makes the whole game feel so much more personal and special.Whether you're new to Ib or a returning player, you're in for a treat. I hope you can enjoy this gem as much as I have!

REVIEW #1422
================================================================================
User: Rasta Koira
Steam ID: 76561198923948156
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 10.8 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 7, 2022

Posted: June 7, 2022
																Finally I'm able to relive my childhood in a higher resolution. I cannot even put into words how much I loved this game as a child, and how much I'll continue to love this game as an adult. However, there was a few points of criticism that emerged during my time with this new version.At times it felt like the game was less scary than the previous version. For example, in the bride puzzle room, I remember the screen turning red and shaking when the painting chowed on the flowers, however it wasn't present in this version.The game also felt quite easy at points. In the orange area, the color-paintings could have been randomized to increase difficulty on subsequent playthroughs. Same could be said for the chest puzzle, and the bird, in the abyssal space.There were positive changes as well. The new puzzles were great. I liked the true exhibit. I feel it adds a lot of replay value. Controversially, I liked Mary's new theme. I felt the music had innocent and even tragic undertones,which probably make the reveal more shocking to new players. Mary's previous theme always felt creepy, which made the player anticipate for the reveal.Overall, I love this game. It's a unique masterpiece with amazing art. 5/5

REVIEW #1423
================================================================================
User: pmemer
Steam ID: 76561198056063859
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 4.0 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 4, 2022

Posted: June 4, 2022
																Ib is a legendary game that everyone should experience at least once. It's one of the most celebrated indie games of the 2010s, and arguably the absolute peak of the RPG maker horror genre. Although Ib always felt more like a creepy tragedy rather than a full blown horror game.The remake takes almost everything that made the original game good, and makes it even better. A few things are changed, the art looks better overall (if a bit less stylised) some puzzles are different and some new stuff was added. The big new feature is the talk button which adds a ton of new dialogue to the game and gives Garry and Mary things to say in each room, and even give hints for certain puzzles. Adds a lot to overall character development.Only complaint is that a handful of puzzles and areas were removed, which is unfortunate as it made the remake a bit shorter and easier. Also they removed the games most iconic song (Puppet) for some reason.

REVIEW #1429
================================================================================
User: blockasen
Steam ID: 76561198346402706
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 22.1 hrs on record
Date: Posted: June 4, 2022

Posted: June 4, 2022
																The Ib Remake still offers that same endearing narrative experience to new players as the original and also makes a good number of changes to surprise older, more familiar fans.The art is as charming as ever, still maintaining the RPG Maker 2003 style while also adding details to sprites from the original. Kouri's new drawings for the game still keep with his iconic style from the original game. All of the art pieces featured in the game are now detailed enough to discern the subjects instead of merely representing a few pixels.The music still uses the iconic YASUPOCHI Guitar Diary arrangements from the original game. Despite the quality of the recordings, they still manage to fit the story beats well emotionally. A lot of the original music has been replaced and don't feel as iconic as their originals, but new additions also seem more appropriate for the narrative than the original's smaller soundtrack.Kouri's writing is still solid. The world of Ib definitely feels like fleshed out with moving parts, characters aren't flat and a lot can be discerned about them and the world they live in from dialogue and environmental objects. A new gameplay feature  that allows players to chat with companions outside of interactable objects  allows players to experience even more of this world building, with it being responsive to real time interactions with the environment or story events.The English translation was solid with minimal typos every now and then. The only arguable negative for this game is its relatively short length. This is, however, made up for in replayability: multiple endings and an optional collectathon on top of Kouri's writing makes paced and slower playthroughs more enjoyable.As a fan of Ib since its rise to cult internet status in the early 2010s, I played the original executable file from a thumb drive in elementary school. With its 2022 remake, I'm happy that Kouri can finally make a consistent profit from their most popular work.

REVIEW #1448

User: Trevbot911

Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 9.4 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 31, 2022

Posted: May 31, 2022
																This is a very different kind of remaster than most of the other RPGmaker horror remasters that have been done.  Rather than just porting the original to the new engine with a few updates and changes while they're at it, this instead takes all of the stuff that made the original memorable and rebuilt the entire game focusing on moments like those.  While a lot of the scares and complex puzzles have either been simplified or removed, all of the art pieces, character interactions, and weird humor are still there with more added to them.  If you mainly liked the horror from the original then you might want to stick with that version but if you liked the story and environments then this is very much worth picking up.

================================================================================
REVIEW #1458
================================================================================
User: casey
Steam ID: 76561198332302327
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 15.5 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 30, 2022

Posted: May 30, 2022
																I'm going to try my best to be brutally honest here, only because I believe all new players and RPG horror veterans alike should understand what they are getting into when considering this version of the game.If, as of reading this sentence, you haven't played the original Ib, go do it. Now.The original Ib is one of the most, if not THE most, titular game of the horror RPG genre. It is compelling, scary, the soundtrack and characters are iconic and lovable in every sense of the word, and most impressively, IT'S FREE. You can go out and download it right now[vgperson.com] and get the same experience that this $13 Steam copy would give you, minus the redundant GUI changes and saddening puzzle removals.So, why am I recommending this game?Well, because I personally don't think this Steam version of the game is bad, but I also don't think it's anything new. My love for Ib and it's developers practically require that I throw my money at them, especially because the original is free and untouched from any new changes.Let's look at a game like The Witch's House compared to The Witch's House MV.The Witch's House was freeware which utilized default RPG Maker VX graphics, and, while dated, the storytelling and simple execution was done as perfectly as it was in it's newer counterpart. So why would I urge you to buy and play The Witch's House MV over it's original? The Witch's House MV not only completely overhauls the outdated graphics, replacing them with beautifully hand-drawn sprites, but rewards the player with a brand new difficulty setting as well, (in the same vain as Mad Father's remake) which expands upon the lore, what made these games so satisfying in the first place.What is different about the original Ib and it's Steam counterpart?(Spoilers ahead, by the way.)The UI for displaying your health is different (personally harder to differentiate). Some of the puzzles have been changed arbitrarily. One of the most iconic songs of the original soundtrack has been completely replaced, assumedly due to licensing issues. There is pop out sprites for dialogue now. A lot of the original sounds have been changed, more often than not to its own detriment (such as the roar when a painting or statue comes to life). The game looks almost completely identical visually. The way the game is now designed has, consequently, become less horror and more drama. The best thing I can give this version is the rework of the talking mechanic, along with a mass of new Garry dialogue.TL;DR Play the free version of Ib here[vgperson.com], if you haven't. If, afterwards, you want to support the developers, as I did, buy this game.

																If you've never played the original, the game is worth buying not only by the fact that it supports the creator. But there is also a couple new endings, the presentation is generally better, and there is more characterization to characters having you enjoy them more. With the puzzles being better than the original.Ok, so if you've played the original Ib. Then yes, I can tell you that the game is worth buying. It's got all the extra content from the original Ib with an added "Press E for Banter" button, that way you can hear what Gary or Mary has to say. The endings also are a lot easier to get than in the original, but it still has a similar style which has the game checking if you've done certain acts in certain amount of times.

REVIEW #1518
================================================================================
User: osmostrix
Steam ID: 76561198107297113
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 9.0 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 21, 2022

Posted: May 21, 2022
																Ib is a simple but compelling experience that embodies some of the more subtle aspects of what I love about games. I played the original years ago as a free, RPG maker game. This version features the unique aspects that made the original so iconic as well as new details that are sure to be enjoyed as well.This experience is defined by completely original, pixel-based artwork. Each one is different and manages to leave a lasting impression on the viewer. From insect specimens, to abstract sculptures, and very many paintings, you will get the unique chance to see all of these pieces while exploring the mysterious, living gallery of the fictional artist Guertena. Meanwhile music serves to communicate the mood of the gallery very delicately while still keeping you entertained. You will be relaxed, amused, and very intrigued by what you see in this very special game!A small note for players who played the original, this game will feature new puzzles and artwork from the original. Most of the experience has been preserved, but some minor elements have been replaced. All of the endings have been kept in this version, so see if you can still figure out how to find them!There are few games as humble as this one that manage to keep your attention, so I highly suggest you purchase it and find out for yourself!

REVIEW #1533
================================================================================
User: Didu
Steam ID: 76561198075462040
Recommendation: Positive
Hours Played: 7.6 hrs on record
Date: Posted: May 19, 2022

Posted: May 19, 2022
Rules of the Art Gallery    No loud conversation.    No photography.    No food or drink.    No touching the displays.    No fountain pens.    No leaving ever.Ib is an absolute classic of its genre and one of my personal all-time favorite games. It's clever, has a great atmosphere and is incredibly memorable. It is a short horror game in which a girl tries to escape a creepy gallery full of living artwork. The variety in concepts used in this gallery and the particular ways in which they spring to life is one of the main appeals I found in it, from creepy to funny to sweet to just, well, clever. It's cast is tiny but interesting and likable, the deadpan, brave little Ib, the soft, gentle and protective Garry and the cheerful but lonely Mary. These characters have stuck with me for years despite the little time the game gives itself to show you what they're about, and the origin of some of them remaining a mystery people still theorize about.  In terms of the remake's changes to the original, the new art is wonderful, showing even more of the characters' personality and detail in the gallery's artwork. The new and replaced puzzles are friendlier than the original, which required to keep pen and paper on hand occasionally. Whether you prefer this simpler kind of puzzle is a matter of taste, I personally enjoyed the note-taking, but the redesigned areas make up for that loss by being full of the particular flavor I loved in the original.The absolute best addition in my eyes though is the dedicated "talk" button to hear your companion's thoughts on any room you're in and the events that occur in them, not only does it work as a subtle hint system to keep you on track if you get lost, but it has a shocking amount of new lines for areas you wouldn't normally visit with a companion at all. The amount of love and care shown here makes the remake even more of an absolute steal.I would recommend this game in a heartbeat to anyone who enjoys horror, and especially to those who liked the era of RPG Maker Horror games, if they somehow managed to miss out on this one.

																I have never written a game review before but I just have to for this game, genuinely one of the most memorable games to ever cross my path about ten years ago and I was so ready to play it again here on Steam. The story, the character, the music, and art and just overall atmosphere of the game is all a 11/10! I first got it and played it on my own in Japanese, and now that the English patch is out I wholeheartedly recommend everyone and anyone interested in Horror RPGs to give this game a chance. There are new puzzles compared to the original version and way more new dialogue this time around! Kouri is an amazing game creator and you feel like the love put into the game. If you want to play or look more into games of this genre, honestly look into Horror RPG Maker Games, there are some that have remakes on Steam and others that are for free out there.
